{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01LCoaWSx8MtpDgBMBBW8Bg7","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01XseKMSTxV8oVyQW9PJe8cr","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Apache Kafka KafkaConsumer API Reference Documentation\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Overview](#overview)\n2. [Core Types](#core-types)\n3. [Consumer Lifecycle](#consumer-lifecycle)\n4. [Subscription and Assignment](#subscription-and-assignment)\n5. [Polling and Data Fetching](#polling-and-data-fetching)\n6. [Offset Management](#offset-management)\n7. [Consumer Group Mechanics](#consumer-group-mechanics)\n8. [Flow Control and Position Management](#flow-control-and-position-management)\n9. [Metadata and Monitoring](#metadata-and-monitoring)\n10. [Error Handling](#error-handling)\n11. [Configuration-Driven Behaviors](#configuration-driven-behaviors)\n12. [Usage Examples](#usage-examples)\n13. [Common Patterns and Best Practices](#common-patterns-and-best-practices)\n\n---\n\n## Overview\n\n### Threading Model\n\nThe Kafka KafkaConsumer is **NOT thread-safe**. All consumer operations must occur within a single consumer thread. The only exception is `wakeup()`, which is explicitly designed to be called from external threads to interrupt blocking operations.\n\n**Key Threading Points:**\n- `KafkaConsumer` maintains an internal event loop that processes rebalances, heartbeats, and data fetches\n- All callbacks (ConsumerRebalanceListener, OffsetCommitCallback) execute within the user's calling thread\n- Concurrent access without synchronization results in `ConcurrentModificationException`\n- The `wakeup()` method is the only safe cross-thread operation\n\n### Consumer Architecture\n\n```\n┌─────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n│  Application Thread                         │\n│  (calls poll(), subscribe(), seek(), etc.)  │\n└──────────────────┬──────────────────────────┘\n                   │\n        ┌──────────▼──────────┐\n        │   KafkaConsumer     │\n        │  (Delegation Layer) │\n        └──────────────────┬──┘\n                           │\n        ┌──────────────────▼──────────────┐\n        │  ConsumerDelegate               │\n        │  (Classic/Async Protocol)       │\n        │  - Rebalance Coordinator        │\n        │  - Fetcher                      │\n        │  - Heartbeat Thread             │\n        │  - Metrics                      │\n        └──────────────────────────────────┘\n```\n\nThe `KafkaConsumer` delegates to a protocol-specific implementation (`ClassicKafkaConsumer` or `AsyncKafkaConsumer`), which manages:\n- Group coordination and rebalancing\n- Heartbeat sending to the broker\n- Fetching records in batches\n- Offset tracking and commits\n\n---\n\n## Core Types\n\n### KafkaConsumer<K, V>\n\nThe main consumer class. Generic over key and value types with deserializers specified in configuration.\n\n```java\n// Constructor variants\nKafkaConsumer(Map<String, Object> configs)\nKafkaConsumer(Properties properties)\nKafkaConsumer(Properties properties, Deserializer<K> keyDeserializer, Deserializer<V> valueDeserializer)\nKafkaConsumer(Map<String, Object> configs, Deserializer<K> keyDeserializer, Deserializer<V> valueDeserializer)\n```\n\n### ConsumerRecord<K, V>\n\nRepresents a single record retrieved from Kafka.\n\n**Key Fields:**\n- `topic()`: Topic name\n- `partition()`: Partition ID\n- `offset()`: Offset within the partition (strictly increasing but may have gaps)\n- `timestamp()`: Message timestamp\n- `timestampType()`: Type of timestamp (CREATE_TIME or LOG_APPEND_TIME)\n- `key()`, `value()`: Deserialized key and value\n- `headers()`: Record headers (mutable collection)\n- `leaderEpoch()`: Optional leader epoch of the record\n\n**Thread Safety Note:** ConsumerRecord is NOT thread-safe. Concurrent access by multiple threads may result in `ConcurrentModificationException` or data corruption.\n\n### ConsumerRecords<K, V>\n\nContainer holding records from a `poll()` call. Partitioned by `TopicPartition`.\n\n**Key Methods:**\n- `records(TopicPartition)`: List of records for a partition\n- `records(String topic)`: Iterable of all records for a topic\n- `partitions()`: Set of partitions with data\n- `nextOffsets()`: Map of next offset and metadata for each partition (the offset to commit)\n- `count()`: Total number of records\n- `isEmpty()`: Whether the collection is empty\n- `iterator()`: Iterate across all records\n\n**Important:** Use `nextOffsets()` when committing offsets after processing, as it contains the correct offset to commit (next record to be read).\n\n### ConsumerRebalanceListener\n\nCallback interface for rebalance events. Must be provided to `subscribe()` for proper offset and state management.\n\n**Methods:**\n- `onPartitionsRevoked(Collection<TopicPartition>)`: Called when partitions are revoked (before rebalance)\n- `onPartitionsAssigned(Collection<TopicPartition>)`: Called when partitions are assigned (after rebalance)\n- `onPartitionsLost(Collection<TopicPartition>)`: Called when partitions are lost without revocation (default delegates to onPartitionsRevoked)\n\n**Execution:** Always called from within the user thread as part of `poll()` during rebalancing.\n\n### OffsetAndMetadata\n\nRepresents a committed offset with optional metadata.\n\n```java\npublic OffsetAndMetadata(long offset)\npublic OffsetAndMetadata(long offset, String metadata)\npublic OffsetAndMetadata(long offset, Optional<Integer> leaderEpoch, String metadata)\n```\n\n**Key Points:**\n- The offset should be the **next offset to read** (one past the last processed message)\n- Leader epoch is optional metadata used for fencing and safety\n- Metadata is user-defined and returned on fetch\n\n### OffsetCommitCallback\n\nFunctional interface for handling async commit completions.\n\n```java\nvoid onComplete(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> offsets, Exception exception);\n```\n\nCalled when a `commitAsync()` request completes, with either success (`exception == null`) or failure.\n\n### GroupProtocol\n\nEnum specifying the group coordination protocol:\n- `CLASSIC`: Original Kafka protocol (eager or cooperative rebalancing)\n- `CONSUMER`: New unified consumer group protocol (always cooperative)\n\n---\n\n## Consumer Lifecycle\n\n### Construction and Initialization\n\n```java\nProperties props = new Properties();\nprops.setProperty(\"bootstrap.servers\", \"localhost:9092\");\nprops.setProperty(\"group.id\", \"my-group\");\nprops.setProperty(\"key.deserializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringDeserializer\");\nprops.setProperty(\"value.deserializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringDeserializer\");\n\nKafkaConsumer<String, String> consumer = new KafkaConsumer<>(props);\n```\n\n**During Construction:**\n- Deserializers are instantiated and configured\n- Metrics are initialized\n- Consumer does NOT immediately join the group (deferred to first `poll()` call)\n\n### Subscription Phase\n\n```java\nconsumer.subscribe(Arrays.asList(\"topic1\", \"topic2\"));\n// or with listener:\nconsumer.subscribe(\n    Arrays.asList(\"topic1\", \"topic2\"),\n    new MyRebalanceListener()\n);\n```\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Subscription is non-incremental (replaces previous subscription)\n- Does not immediately join the group\n- Metadata fetching for subscribed topics begins in the background\n- Empty subscription list is equivalent to `unsubscribe()`\n\n### Group Membership Join\n\nThe consumer joins the group on the **first `poll()` call**, not during `subscribe()`.\n\n```java\n// Group join happens here:\nConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n```\n\n**Join Process:**\n1. Metadata refresh to find broker\n2. FindCoordinator request to locate the group coordinator\n3. JoinGroup request to join the group\n4. SyncGroup request to receive partition assignment\n5. Rebalance callbacks invoked (if listener provided)\n\n### Closing and Resource Cleanup\n\n```java\nconsumer.close();\n// or with timeout:\nconsumer.close(Duration.ofSeconds(30));\n// or with options:\nconsumer.close(CloseOptions.builder().timeout(Duration.ofSeconds(30)).build());\n```\n\n**Close Behavior:**\n- Revokes assigned partitions (calls `onPartitionsRevoked()` on listener)\n- Commits offsets if `enable.auto.commit` is true and offset tracking is enabled\n- Closes all broker connections\n- Interrupts all internal threads\n- Timeout applies to graceful shutdown; after timeout, unclean shutdown occurs\n\n---\n\n## Subscription and Assignment\n\n### Dynamic Assignment via Subscription\n\n**Methods:**\n```java\n// List of topics\nvoid subscribe(Collection<String> topics)\nvoid subscribe(Collection<String> topics, ConsumerRebalanceListener listener)\n\n// Pattern matching (periodic refresh)\nvoid subscribe(Pattern pattern)\nvoid subscribe(Pattern pattern, ConsumerRebalanceListener listener)\n\n// Google RE2/J compatible pattern (CONSUMER protocol only)\nvoid subscribe(SubscriptionPattern pattern)\nvoid subscribe(SubscriptionPattern pattern, ConsumerRebalanceListener listener)\n```\n\n**Key Characteristics:**\n- Enables automatic load balancing across consumer group members\n- Rebalancing occurs when:\n  - Partitions added to/removed from subscribed topics\n  - Consumer joins/leaves group\n  - Consumer crashes/disconnects\n- Rebalancing is **only detected and triggered during `poll()`**\n- Pattern subscriptions refresh metadata periodically (controlled by `metadata.max.age.ms`)\n\n**Incompatibility:** Cannot mix `subscribe()` and `assign()` without calling `unsubscribe()` first.\n\n### Manual Assignment\n\n**Method:**\n```java\nvoid assign(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions)\n```\n\n**Characteristics:**\n- Static partition assignment without group coordination\n- Suitable for:\n  - Stateful processing where local state is associated with partitions\n  - Standalone consumers that don't need rebalancing\n  - Custom assignment logic\n- Partition changes only occur on explicit `assign()` calls\n- Offset management still uses group membership for commits (but can be standalone)\n\n**Example:**\n```java\nconsumer.assign(Arrays.asList(\n    new TopicPartition(\"topic\", 0),\n    new TopicPartition(\"topic\", 1)\n));\n```\n\n### Unsubscribe\n\n```java\nvoid unsubscribe()\n```\n\nRemoves all subscriptions and assignments. The next `poll()` will return immediately with no records.\n\n---\n\n## Polling and Data Fetching\n\n### poll(Duration timeout)\n\n```java\nConsumerRecords<K, V> poll(Duration timeout)\n```\n\n**Semantics:**\n- Fetches records from assigned partitions\n- Returns immediately if records are available\n- Blocks for up to `timeout` duration if no records available\n- **May block longer than timeout** if a rebalance is triggered\n- Executes rebalance callbacks if rebalancing occurs\n- Sends heartbeats to maintain group membership\n- Automatically refreshes metadata when needed\n- Can throw `WakeupException` if `wakeup()` called\n\n**Return Value:**\n- `ConsumerRecords` containing fetched records partitioned by `TopicPartition`\n- Empty `ConsumerRecords` if no data available (timeout expired, or empty assignment)\n- Records from paused partitions are excluded\n\n**Important Behaviors:**\n\n1. **Rebalance Callbacks During Poll**\n   - If a rebalance is detected, callbacks execute **within the `poll()` call**\n   - Rebalance can occur at any point during poll processing\n   - Callbacks may block arbitrary durations\n   - `poll()` only returns after rebalance completes\n\n2. **Max Records Limiting**\n   - `max.poll.records` configuration limits the batch size\n   - Useful for predictable processing time windows\n   - Default is 500 records\n\n3. **Offset Advancement**\n   - Position advances as records are returned\n   - Position = offset of next record to be returned\n   - NOT advanced if record is returned but not processed\n   - Automatic commits occur relative to position\n\n### poll() Loop Requirements\n\nTo maintain group membership, you **MUST call `poll()` frequently**:\n- At least once every `max.poll.interval.ms` (default: 5 minutes)\n- If not called within this interval, the consumer proactively leaves the group\n- Subsequent `commitSync()` calls fail with `CommitFailedException`\n\n```java\n// RECOMMENDED: Keep poll interval tight for responsiveness\ntry {\n    while (true) {\n        ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n        for (ConsumerRecord<String, String> record : records) {\n            // Fast processing only\n            processRecord(record);\n        }\n        consumer.commitSync();\n    }\n} catch (WakeupException e) {\n    // Expected on shutdown\n} finally {\n    consumer.close();\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Offset Management\n\n### Offset Concepts\n\n**Position** (consumer's current position):\n- Offset of the next record to be fetched\n- Automatically advanced by `poll()`\n- Can be queried with `position(TopicPartition)`\n- Can be moved with `seek(TopicPartition, long)`\n\n**Committed Offset**:\n- Last offset stored in the broker for the partition\n- Used as the starting position on consumer restart\n- Committed via `commitSync()` or `commitAsync()`\n- Queried with `committed(Set<TopicPartition>)`\n\n**Relationship:**\n- Committed offset should be **next offset to read** (one past the last processed message)\n- If position > committed: records haven't been committed yet\n- If position < committed: some records were skipped\n\n### Offset Commit Strategies\n\n#### Automatic Committing\n\n**Configuration:**\n```properties\nenable.auto.commit=true\nauto.commit.interval.ms=1000\n```\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Offsets committed periodically (every `auto.commit.interval.ms`)\n- Committed offset = current position at commit time\n- Non-blocking (background operation)\n- Risk: Can commit offsets before records are processed\n\n**Suitable For:**\n- Simple use cases with fast, reliable processing\n- \"At-least-once\" delivery with automatic retry\n\n#### Synchronous Commits\n\n```java\nconsumer.commitSync()\nconsumer.commitSync(Duration.ofSeconds(10))\nconsumer.commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> offsets)\nconsumer.commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> offsets, Duration timeout)\n```\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Blocks until commit succeeds or fails\n- Retries transient failures\n- Throws `CommitFailedException` if consumer lost group membership\n- Throws `TimeoutException` if operation exceeds timeout\n- May fail with `RebalanceInProgressException` during rebalance\n\n**Suitable For:**\n- Exact-once or at-least-once processing with external state\n- Batched processing where records are buffered before commit\n- Custom offset stores\n\n**Best Practice:**\n```java\nwhile (running) {\n    ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n    List<String> batch = new ArrayList<>();\n\n    for (ConsumerRecord<String, String> record : records) {\n        batch.add(record.value());\n    }\n\n    if (!batch.isEmpty()) {\n        // Process batch\n        processBatch(batch);\n\n        // Commit only after successful processing\n        try {\n            consumer.commitSync();\n        } catch (CommitFailedException e) {\n            // Handle: consumer lost partitions\n            break;\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### Asynchronous Commits\n\n```java\nconsumer.commitAsync()\nconsumer.commitAsync(OffsetCommitCallback callback)\nconsumer.commitAsync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> offsets, OffsetCommitCallback callback)\n```\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns immediately without waiting for broker response\n- Callback invoked asynchronously when request completes\n- Callback may execute in any thread (typically the poll thread)\n- Earlier async commits may be superseded by later ones\n\n**Callback Signature:**\n```java\nvoid onComplete(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> offsets, Exception exception)\n```\n\n**Suitable For:**\n- High-throughput scenarios\n- Combining with synchronous commits for periodic safety\n\n**Pattern (Async + Periodic Sync):**\n```java\nint commitInterval = 100;\nint recordCount = 0;\n\nwhile (running) {\n    ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n\n    for (ConsumerRecord<String, String> record : records) {\n        processRecord(record);\n        recordCount++;\n\n        // Async commit frequently for progress\n        if (recordCount % commitInterval == 0) {\n            consumer.commitAsync((offsets, exception) -> {\n                if (exception != null) {\n                    logger.error(\"Async commit failed\", exception);\n                }\n            });\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Periodic sync commits for safety\n    if (recordCount % (commitInterval * 10) == 0) {\n        try {\n            consumer.commitSync();\n        } catch (CommitFailedException e) {\n            logger.error(\"Sync commit failed\", e);\n            break;\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Offset Queries and Seeking\n\n#### Query Committed Offset\n\n```java\nMap<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> committed(Set<TopicPartition> partitions)\nMap<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> committed(Set<TopicPartition> partitions, Duration timeout)\n```\n\nReturns the last committed offset for each partition. Useful on initialization to resume from the last committed position.\n\n#### Query Current Position\n\n```java\nlong position(TopicPartition partition)\nlong position(TopicPartition partition, Duration timeout)\n```\n\nReturns the offset of the next record to be fetched.\n\n#### Seek Operations\n\n```java\nvoid seek(TopicPartition partition, long offset)\nvoid seek(TopicPartition partition, OffsetAndMetadata offsetAndMetadata)\nvoid seekToBeginning(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions)\nvoid seekToEnd(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions)\n```\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Changes the consumer's position for future `poll()` calls\n- Does not fetch records immediately\n- Effect visible on next `poll()`\n- `seekToBeginning`: Seeks to oldest available record\n- `seekToEnd`: Seeks to end of partition\n\n**Special Case - read_committed Isolation:**\n- With `isolation.level=read_committed`, `endOffsets()` returns the Last Stable Offset (LSO)\n- LSO is the offset of the first message in an open transaction\n- `seekToEnd()` seeks to LSO, not the true end\n- Transactional messages and abort markers are filtered out\n\n#### Offset-to-Timestamp Lookup\n\n```java\nMap<TopicPartition, OffsetAndTimestamp> offsetsForTimes(Map<TopicPartition, Long> timestampsToSearch)\nMap<TopicPartition, OffsetAndTimestamp> offsetsForTimes(Map<TopicPartition, Long> timestampsToSearch, Duration timeout)\n```\n\nReturns the offset with a timestamp >= the specified timestamp for each partition. Useful for time-based seeking.\n\n**Example:**\n```java\n// Seek to records from 5 minutes ago\nlong fiveMinutesAgo = System.currentTimeMillis() - 5 * 60 * 1000;\nMap<TopicPartition, Long> timestamps = new HashMap<>();\nfor (TopicPartition tp : consumer.assignment()) {\n    timestamps.put(tp, fiveMinutesAgo);\n}\n\nMap<TopicPartition, OffsetAndTimestamp> offsets = consumer.offsetsForTimes(timestamps);\nfor (Map.Entry<TopicPartition, OffsetAndTimestamp> entry : offsets.entrySet()) {\n    if (entry.getValue() != null) {\n        consumer.seek(entry.getKey(), entry.getValue().offset());\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### External Offset Storage\n\nFor \"exactly-once\" semantics with atomic processing, store offsets alongside results:\n\n```java\nwhile (running) {\n    ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n\n    // Store records and offsets atomically in external system\n    for (ConsumerRecord<String, String> record : records) {\n        database.storeResult(\n            processRecord(record),\n            record.offset()\n        );\n    }\n\n    // Committed offset will be persisted by the database transaction\n}\n```\n\nResume from external offset on restart:\n```java\nconsumer.assign(partitions);\n\nfor (TopicPartition tp : partitions) {\n    long lastOffset = database.getLastOffset(tp);\n    if (lastOffset >= 0) {\n        consumer.seek(tp, lastOffset);\n    } else {\n        consumer.seekToBeginning(Collections.singletonList(tp));\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Consumer Group Mechanics\n\n### Group Membership and Coordination\n\n**Group Concept:**\n- Logical aggregation of consumers with the same `group.id`\n- One consumer group can have multiple members\n- Each partition assigned to exactly one member (for load balancing)\n\n**Lifecycle:**\n1. **Init**: Consumer created but not in group\n2. **Join**: First `poll()` triggers join via JoinGroup request\n3. **Sync**: Broker coordinates partition assignment\n4. **Stable**: Member receives partitions and starts fetching\n5. **Rebalancing**: Triggered by membership or subscription changes\n6. **Revocation**: Member gives up partitions (calls `onPartitionsRevoked`)\n7. **Assignment**: Member receives new partitions (calls `onPartitionsAssigned`)\n\n### Rebalancing Details\n\n**Rebalancing is triggered when:**\n- New member joins group\n- Existing member leaves/crashes\n- Subscription changes (new topics match pattern)\n- Topic partitions change\n- Consumer calls `enforceRebalance()`\n\n**Detection and Execution:**\n- Rebalancing is **ONLY** detected during `poll()` calls\n- Once detected, callbacks execute immediately within `poll()`\n- No `poll()` called = no rebalance detection = potential stale assignment\n\n**Rebalance Protocols:**\n\n**Classic Protocol (Eager):**\n- All members revoke partitions simultaneously\n- `onPartitionsRevoked()` called with full assignment\n- All members wait for synchronization\n- Then all receive new assignments\n- Higher stop-the-world pause time\n- Higher latency during rebalance\n\n**Classic Protocol (Cooperative):**\n- Members retain partitions where possible\n- Only revoked partitions are given up\n- `onPartitionsRevoked()` called with minimal set\n- Reduces stop-the-world pause\n- Requires compatible assignors\n\n**Consumer Protocol (New):**\n- Always cooperative rebalancing\n- Incremental partition migration\n- Lowest downtime during rebalance\n\n**Rebalance Callback Guarantees:**\n- `onPartitionsRevoked()` is called before partition move\n- `onPartitionsAssigned()` is called after partition is acquired\n- During normal rebalance: revoked → new_owner_assigned guaranteed ordering\n- Exception scenarios: partition may be lost without revoke → `onPartitionsLost()` called\n- `onPartitionsAssigned()` always called (even if empty list)\n\n### Heartbeating and Session Management\n\n**Session Timeout** (`session.timeout.ms`, default: 10 seconds):\n- If broker receives no heartbeat for this duration, consumer is removed\n- Other members detect removal and rebalance\n\n**Max Poll Interval** (`max.poll.interval.ms`, default: 5 minutes):\n- If `poll()` not called for this duration, consumer proactively leaves\n- Prevents livelock: consumer continues heartbeating but makes no progress\n- Subsequent commits fail with `CommitFailedException`\n\n**Heartbeat Thread:**\n- Background thread sends heartbeats periodically\n- Interval controlled by `heartbeat.interval.ms` (default: 3 seconds)\n- Runs independently of main consumer thread\n\n**Practical Implications:**\n```java\n// GOOD: Tight poll loop maintains membership\nwhile (running) {\n    ConsumerRecords records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));  // ✓ Called frequently\n    for (ConsumerRecord record : records) {\n        processRecord(record);  // Fast processing\n    }\n}\n\n// BAD: Slow processing causes member removal\nwhile (running) {\n    ConsumerRecords records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofSeconds(30));\n    for (ConsumerRecord record : records) {\n        slowProcess(record);  // ✗ Can exceed max.poll.interval.ms\n    }\n}\n\n// BETTER: Offload processing to thread pool\nwhile (running) {\n    ConsumerRecords records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n    for (ConsumerRecord record : records) {\n        executor.submit(() -> processRecord(record));  // Non-blocking\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Enforcing Rebalance\n\n```java\nvoid enforceRebalance()\nvoid enforceRebalance(String reason)\n```\n\nManually trigger a rebalance on next `poll()`. Useful for:\n- Graceful shutdown with immediate state flush\n- Redistribution of partitions\n- Internal consumer state reconciliation\n\n---\n\n## Flow Control and Position Management\n\n### Pause and Resume\n\n**Methods:**\n```java\nvoid pause(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions)\nvoid resume(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions)\nSet<TopicPartition> paused()\n```\n\n**Behavior:**\n- `pause()`: Excludes partitions from future `poll()` calls\n- Position is NOT reset (unchanged when resumed)\n- Useful for flow control or batching\n- Multiple pauses for different partitions are independent\n- `paused()` returns the current set of paused partitions\n\n**Use Case - Processing Coordination:**\n```java\n// Pause fast partition to let slow partition catch up in join\nfor (TopicPartition tp : consumer.assignment()) {\n    long lag = endOffset - position(tp);\n    if (lag > 100000) {\n        consumer.resume(Collections.singletonList(tp));\n    } else {\n        consumer.pause(Collections.singletonList(tp));\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Current Lag\n\n```java\nOptionalLong currentLag(TopicPartition partition)\n```\n\nReturns the difference between high water mark and consumer position. Useful for monitoring consumption progress.\n\n---\n\n## Metadata and Monitoring\n\n### Partition Information\n\n```java\nList<PartitionInfo> partitionsFor(String topic)\nList<PartitionInfo> partitionsFor(String topic, Duration timeout)\nMap<String, List<PartitionInfo>> listTopics()\nMap<String, List<PartitionInfo>> listTopics(Duration timeout)\n```\n\nFetch metadata about topics and partitions. Blocking operations with optional timeout.\n\n### Metrics\n\n```java\nMap<MetricName, ? extends Metric> metrics()\n```\n\nReturns all metrics being collected for this consumer. Useful for monitoring via JMX or custom collectors.\n\nCommon metrics:\n- `fetch-total-bytes`\n- `fetch-total-records`\n- `records-lag-max`\n- `records-consumed-total`\n- `record-lag`\n\n### Group Metadata\n\n```java\nConsumerGroupMetadata groupMetadata()\n```\n\nReturns metadata about current group membership. Used in producer for transactional producing.\n\n### Client Instance ID\n\n```java\nUuid clientInstanceId(Duration timeout)\n```\n\nUnique identifier for this consumer instance. Used by brokers for tracking and fencing.\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### CommitFailedException\n\n**Thrown by:** `commitSync()`, `commitAsync()` callback\n\n**Cause:**\n- Consumer is no longer part of the group\n- Consumer didn't call `poll()` within `max.poll.interval.ms`\n- Consumer was fenced by another member\n- Group coordinator changed (rare)\n\n**Recovery:**\n- Stop committing and exit consumer loop\n- Optionally notify external state manager\n- Close consumer and rejoin group\n\n```java\ntry {\n    consumer.commitSync();\n} catch (CommitFailedException e) {\n    logger.error(\"Lost group membership, exiting\", e);\n    break;  // Exit loop\n}\n```\n\n### RetriableCommitFailedException\n\n**Thrown by:** `commitSync()` callback with automatic retry\n\n**Cause:**\n- Broker not available\n- Coordinator not stable\n- Other transient failures\n\n**Behavior:**\n- `commitSync()` automatically retries\n- `commitAsync()` only notifies callback, no retry\n- Not fatal - can retry manually after wait\n\n### WakeupException\n\n**Thrown by:** `poll()`, `commitSync()`, `commitAsync()` if `wakeup()` called\n\n**Use:**\n- Signal to interrupt blocking operations\n- Allows shutdown from another thread\n- Not an error condition (expected on shutdown)\n\n**Handling:**\n```java\ntry {\n    while (true) {\n        consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n    }\n} catch (WakeupException e) {\n    logger.info(\"Consumer woken up, shutting down\");\n    // Expected on shutdown\n} finally {\n    consumer.close();\n}\n```\n\n### InterruptException\n\n**Thrown by:** Operations if consumer thread's interrupt flag is set\n\n**Cause:**\n- Another thread called `Thread.interrupt()` on consumer thread\n- Not preferred method (use `wakeup()` instead)\n\n### Offset Exceptions\n\n**NoOffsetForPartitionException:**\n- No committed offset found and `auto.offset.reset` is \"none\"\n\n**OffsetOutOfRangeException:**\n- Seek position is before earliest or after latest offset\n- Consumer resets position based on `auto.offset.reset` strategy\n\n**InvalidOffsetException:**\n- Offset is invalid (negative, non-existent)\n\n**LogTruncationException:**\n- Partition was truncated and committed offset was lost\n- Consumer must reset position manually\n\n### Deserialization Failures\n\n**RecordDeserializationException:**\n- Key or value deserialization fails\n- Error contains the problematic record offset and topic\n- Consumer skips the record and continues\n\n**Handling:**\n```java\ntry {\n    while (true) {\n        ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n        for (ConsumerRecord<String, String> record : records) {\n            try {\n                processRecord(record);\n            } catch (RecordDeserializationException e) {\n                logger.error(\"Deserialization failed for {}-{}, skipping\",\n                    e.topicPartition(), e.offset(), e);\n                // Record skipped, continue to next\n            }\n        }\n    }\n} catch (WakeupException e) {\n    // Shutdown\n} finally {\n    consumer.close();\n}\n```\n\n### Authentication/Authorization Errors\n\n**AuthenticationException:**\n- Broker rejected credentials\n- Check bootstrap.servers, sasl.jaas.config, etc.\n\n**AuthorizationException:**\n- Principal not authorized for topic/consumer group\n- Check ACLs and permissions\n\n### Broker-Level Errors\n\n**FencedInstanceIdException:**\n- Another member with the same `client.id` joined (classic protocol)\n- Consumer instance was fenced by broker\n- Fatal - must close and rejoin\n\n**TimeoutException:**\n- Operation exceeded configured timeout\n- Broker might be slow or unreachable\n- Safe to retry (is transient)\n\n---\n\n## Configuration-Driven Behaviors\n\n### Key Configurations Affecting API Behavior\n\n#### Offset Commit Behavior\n- `enable.auto.commit`: Enable/disable automatic offset commits (default: true)\n- `auto.commit.interval.ms`: Frequency of automatic commits (default: 5000ms)\n- `offsets.retention.minutes`: How long offsets are retained (default: 10080 minutes = 7 days)\n\n#### Group Membership\n- `session.timeout.ms`: Broker timeout for detection (default: 10000ms)\n- `heartbeat.interval.ms`: Heartbeat frequency (default: 3000ms)\n- `max.poll.interval.ms`: Maximum time between polls (default: 300000ms)\n- `max.poll.records`: Maximum records per poll (default: 500)\n\n#### Group Protocol\n- `group.protocol`: Protocol version (\"classic\", \"consumer\") - default: \"consumer\"\n- `partition.assignment.strategy`: Assignor list (default: [\"RangeAssignor\"])\n  - RangeAssignor: Partitions assigned in ranges\n  - RoundRobinAssignor: Partitions distributed round-robin\n  - StickyAssignor: Minimize partition movement\n  - CooperativeStickyAssignor: Sticky with cooperative rebalancing\n\n#### Fetch and Network\n- `fetch.min.bytes`: Minimum bytes before returning (default: 1)\n- `fetch.max.wait.ms`: Maximum wait for fetch.min.bytes (default: 500ms)\n- `fetch.max.bytes`: Maximum bytes per fetch (default: 52428800 = 50MB)\n- `max.partition.fetch.bytes`: Maximum per partition (default: 1048576 = 1MB)\n\n#### Isolation and Transactions\n- `isolation.level`: \"read_uncommitted\" or \"read_committed\" (default: read_uncommitted)\n  - With read_committed: filters aborted transactions, reads up to LSO\n  - With read_uncommitted: reads all committed + uncommitted messages\n\n#### Metadata\n- `metadata.max.age.ms`: Metadata refresh interval (default: 300000ms)\n- `topic.metadata.refresh.interval.ms`: Topic-specific refresh (default: -1, use metadata.max.age.ms)\n\n#### Timeouts\n- `default.api.timeout.ms`: Default timeout for most operations (default: 60000ms)\n- `connections.max.idle.ms`: Idle connection timeout (default: 540000ms)\n\n### Example: Tight Poll Loop Configuration\n\n```properties\n# Fast response times\nmax.poll.records=100\nfetch.min.bytes=1\nfetch.max.wait.ms=100\n\n# Long offset retention for recovery\noffsets.retention.minutes=40320  # 28 days\n\n# Strict session management\nsession.timeout.ms=6000\nheartbeat.interval.ms=2000\nmax.poll.interval.ms=30000\n\n# Cooperative rebalancing to minimize stop-the-world\ngroup.protocol=consumer\npartition.assignment.strategy=org.apache.kafka.clients.consumer.CooperativeStickyAssignor\n```\n\n---\n\n## Usage Examples\n\n### Example 1: Basic Subscription with Automatic Commits\n\n```java\npublic class AutoCommitConsumer {\n    public static void main(String[] args) {\n        Properties props = new Properties();\n        props.setProperty(\"bootstrap.servers\", \"localhost:9092\");\n        props.setProperty(\"group.id\", \"my-group\");\n        props.setProperty(\"enable.auto.commit\", \"true\");\n        props.setProperty(\"auto.commit.interval.ms\", \"1000\");\n        props.setProperty(\"key.deserializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringDeserializer\");\n        props.setProperty(\"value.deserializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringDeserializer\");\n\n        KafkaConsumer<String, String> consumer = new KafkaConsumer<>(props);\n        consumer.subscribe(Arrays.asList(\"my-topic\"));\n\n        try {\n            while (true) {\n                ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n                for (ConsumerRecord<String, String> record : records) {\n                    System.out.printf(\n                        \"offset = %d, key = %s, value = %s%n\",\n                        record.offset(),\n                        record.key(),\n                        record.value()\n                    );\n                }\n            }\n        } finally {\n            consumer.close();\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Example 2: Manual Offset Control with Batch Processing\n\n```java\npublic class ManualCommitConsumer {\n    public static void main(String[] args) {\n        Properties props = new Properties();\n        props.setProperty(\"bootstrap.servers\", \"localhost:9092\");\n        props.setProperty(\"group.id\", \"batch-group\");\n        props.setProperty(\"enable.auto.commit\", \"false\");  // Manual commits\n        props.setProperty(\"key.deserializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringDeserializer\");\n        props.setProperty(\"value.deserializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringDeserializer\");\n\n        KafkaConsumer<String, String> consumer = new KafkaConsumer<>(props);\n        consumer.subscribe(Arrays.asList(\"my-topic\"));\n\n        List<ConsumerRecord<String, String>> buffer = new ArrayList<>();\n        int batchSize = 100;\n\n        try {\n            while (true) {\n                ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n\n                for (ConsumerRecord<String, String> record : records) {\n                    buffer.add(record);\n                }\n\n                // Batch processing\n                if (buffer.size() >= batchSize) {\n                    processBatch(buffer);\n                    buffer.clear();\n\n                    // Commit only after successful processing\n                    try {\n                        consumer.commitSync();\n                        System.out.println(\"Offsets committed\");\n                    } catch (CommitFailedException e) {\n                        System.err.println(\"Commit failed - consumer lost partitions\");\n                        break;\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n        } finally {\n            consumer.close();\n        }\n    }\n\n    static void processBatch(List<ConsumerRecord<String, String>> records) {\n        // Simulate batch processing\n        System.out.println(\"Processing batch of \" + records.size() + \" records\");\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Example 3: Rebalance Listener with Custom Offset Management\n\n```java\npublic class RebalanceListenerExample {\n    static class SaveOffsetsOnRebalance implements ConsumerRebalanceListener {\n        private KafkaConsumer<String, String> consumer;\n        private Map<TopicPartition, Long> offsetStore = new HashMap<>();\n\n        public SaveOffsetsOnRebalance(KafkaConsumer<String, String> consumer) {\n            this.consumer = consumer;\n        }\n\n        @Override\n        public void onPartitionsRevoked(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\n            // Save offsets to external store\n            for (TopicPartition partition : partitions) {\n                long offset = consumer.position(partition);\n                offsetStore.put(partition, offset);\n                System.out.println(\"Revoked \" + partition + \" at offset \" + offset);\n            }\n        }\n\n        @Override\n        public void onPartitionsAssigned(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\n            // Restore offsets from external store\n            for (TopicPartition partition : partitions) {\n                Long offset = offsetStore.getOrDefault(partition, 0L);\n                consumer.seek(partition, offset);\n                System.out.println(\"Assigned \" + partition + \" at offset \" + offset);\n            }\n        }\n\n        @Override\n        public void onPartitionsLost(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\n            // Partitions lost without revoke - don't save offsets\n            System.out.println(\"Lost partitions: \" + partitions);\n        }\n    }\n\n    public static void main(String[] args) {\n        Properties props = new Properties();\n        props.setProperty(\"bootstrap.servers\", \"localhost:9092\");\n        props.setProperty(\"group.id\", \"rebalance-group\");\n        props.setProperty(\"enable.auto.commit\", \"false\");\n        props.setProperty(\"key.deserializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringDeserializer\");\n        props.setProperty(\"value.deserializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringDeserializer\");\n\n        KafkaConsumer<String, String> consumer = new KafkaConsumer<>(props);\n        ConsumerRebalanceListener rebalanceListener = new SaveOffsetsOnRebalance(consumer);\n\n        consumer.subscribe(Arrays.asList(\"my-topic\"), rebalanceListener);\n\n        try {\n            while (true) {\n                ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n                for (ConsumerRecord<String, String> record : records) {\n                    System.out.println(\"Processing: \" + record.value());\n                }\n\n                // Commit current offsets\n                if (records.count() > 0) {\n                    consumer.commitSync();\n                }\n            }\n        } catch (WakeupException e) {\n            // Shutdown\n        } finally {\n            consumer.close();\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Example 4: Partition-Specific Commits\n\n```java\npublic class PartitionSpecificCommit {\n    public static void main(String[] args) {\n        Properties props = new Properties();\n        props.setProperty(\"bootstrap.servers\", \"localhost:9092\");\n        props.setProperty(\"group.id\", \"partition-group\");\n        props.setProperty(\"enable.auto.commit\", \"false\");\n        props.setProperty(\"key.deserializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringDeserializer\");\n        props.setProperty(\"value.deserializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringDeserializer\");\n\n        KafkaConsumer<String, String> consumer = new KafkaConsumer<>(props);\n        consumer.subscribe(Arrays.asList(\"my-topic\"));\n\n        try {\n            while (true) {\n                ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n\n                // Process records and commit per partition\n                for (TopicPartition partition : records.partitions()) {\n                    List<ConsumerRecord<String, String>> partitionRecords = records.records(partition);\n\n                    for (ConsumerRecord<String, String> record : partitionRecords) {\n                        System.out.println(\"Processing: \" + record.value());\n                    }\n\n                    // Commit the next offset for this partition\n                    long nextOffset = partitionRecords.get(partitionRecords.size() - 1).offset() + 1;\n                    consumer.commitSync(\n                        Collections.singletonMap(\n                            partition,\n                            new OffsetAndMetadata(nextOffset)\n                        )\n                    );\n                }\n            }\n        } finally {\n            consumer.close();\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Example 5: Seeking and Time-Based Consumption\n\n```java\npublic class SeekExample {\n    public static void main(String[] args) {\n        Properties props = new Properties();\n        props.setProperty(\"bootstrap.servers\", \"localhost:9092\");\n        props.setProperty(\"group.id\", \"seek-group\");\n        props.setProperty(\"key.deserializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringDeserializer\");\n        props.setProperty(\"value.deserializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringDeserializer\");\n\n        KafkaConsumer<String, String> consumer = new KafkaConsumer<>(props);\n\n        // Manual assignment instead of subscription\n        TopicPartition partition = new TopicPartition(\"my-topic\", 0);\n        consumer.assign(Collections.singletonList(partition));\n\n        // Seek to beginning\n        consumer.seekToBeginning(Collections.singletonList(partition));\n\n        // Or seek to specific offset\n        consumer.seek(partition, 100);\n\n        // Or seek to timestamp (5 minutes ago)\n        long timestamp = System.currentTimeMillis() - 5 * 60 * 1000;\n        Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndTimestamp> offsets = consumer.offsetsForTimes(\n            Collections.singletonMap(partition, timestamp)\n        );\n        if (offsets.get(partition) != null) {\n            consumer.seek(partition, offsets.get(partition).offset());\n        }\n\n        try {\n            while (true) {\n                ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n                for (ConsumerRecord<String, String> record : records) {\n                    System.out.printf(\n                        \"Offset: %d, Timestamp: %d, Value: %s%n\",\n                        record.offset(),\n                        record.timestamp(),\n                        record.value()\n                    );\n                }\n            }\n        } finally {\n            consumer.close();\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Example 6: Multi-Threaded Processing with Wakeup\n\n```java\npublic class MultiThreadedConsumer implements Runnable {\n    private final KafkaConsumer<String, String> consumer;\n    private final AtomicBoolean shutdown = new AtomicBoolean(false);\n    private final ExecutorService executor = Executors.newFixedThreadPool(4);\n\n    public MultiThreadedConsumer() {\n        Properties props = new Properties();\n        props.setProperty(\"bootstrap.servers\", \"localhost:9092\");\n        props.setProperty(\"group.id\", \"multithreaded-group\");\n        props.setProperty(\"enable.auto.commit\", \"false\");\n        props.setProperty(\"max.poll.records\", \"10\");\n        props.setProperty(\"key.deserializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringDeserializer\");\n        props.setProperty(\"value.deserializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringDeserializer\");\n\n        this.consumer = new KafkaConsumer<>(props);\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void run() {\n        try {\n            consumer.subscribe(Arrays.asList(\"my-topic\"));\n\n            while (!shutdown.get()) {\n                ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(1000));\n\n                // Submit records to thread pool for processing\n                for (ConsumerRecord<String, String> record : records) {\n                    executor.submit(() -> {\n                        try {\n                            processRecord(record);\n                        } catch (Exception e) {\n                            System.err.println(\"Processing failed: \" + e.getMessage());\n                        }\n                    });\n                }\n\n                // Commit asynchronously\n                if (records.count() > 0) {\n                    consumer.commitAsync((offsets, exception) -> {\n                        if (exception != null) {\n                            System.err.println(\"Async commit failed: \" + exception.getMessage());\n                        }\n                    });\n                }\n            }\n        } catch (WakeupException e) {\n            // Expected during shutdown\n        } finally {\n            try {\n                // Wait for in-flight tasks\n                executor.shutdown();\n                executor.awaitTermination(10, TimeUnit.SECONDS);\n\n                // Final sync commit\n                consumer.commitSync();\n            } catch (Exception e) {\n                System.err.println(\"Shutdown error: \" + e.getMessage());\n            } finally {\n                consumer.close();\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    private void processRecord(ConsumerRecord<String, String> record) {\n        // Simulate processing\n        Thread.sleep(10);\n        System.out.println(\"Processed: \" + record.value());\n    }\n\n    public void shutdown() {\n        shutdown.set(true);\n        consumer.wakeup();\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Example 7: Read Committed Isolation for Transactions\n\n```java\npublic class TransactionalConsumer {\n    public static void main(String[] args) {\n        Properties props = new Properties();\n        props.setProperty(\"bootstrap.servers\", \"localhost:9092\");\n        props.setProperty(\"group.id\", \"transactional-group\");\n        props.setProperty(\"isolation.level\", \"read_committed\");  // Only committed messages\n        props.setProperty(\"enable.auto.commit\", \"false\");\n        props.setProperty(\"key.deserializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringDeserializer\");\n        props.setProperty(\"value.deserializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringDeserializer\");\n\n        KafkaConsumer<String, String> consumer = new KafkaConsumer<>(props);\n        consumer.subscribe(Arrays.asList(\"transactional-topic\"));\n\n        try {\n            while (true) {\n                ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n\n                for (ConsumerRecord<String, String> record : records) {\n                    // Only receives committed/non-aborted messages\n                    System.out.printf(\n                        \"Safe record: offset=%d, value=%s%n\",\n                        record.offset(),\n                        record.value()\n                    );\n                }\n\n                if (records.count() > 0) {\n                    consumer.commitSync();\n                }\n            }\n        } catch (WakeupException e) {\n            // Shutdown\n        } finally {\n            consumer.close();\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Common Patterns and Best Practices\n\n### Pattern 1: Graceful Shutdown\n\n```java\npublic class GracefulShutdown {\n    public static void main(String[] args) {\n        KafkaConsumer<String, String> consumer = createConsumer();\n\n        // Register shutdown hook\n        Runtime.getRuntime().addShutdownHook(new Thread(() -> {\n            System.out.println(\"Shutting down consumer\");\n            consumer.wakeup();\n        }));\n\n        try {\n            while (true) {\n                ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n                for (ConsumerRecord<String, String> record : records) {\n                    processRecord(record);\n                }\n                consumer.commitAsync();\n            }\n        } catch (WakeupException e) {\n            System.out.println(\"Consumer woken up\");\n        } finally {\n            try {\n                consumer.commitSync();  // Final sync commit\n                System.out.println(\"Offsets committed\");\n            } catch (CommitFailedException e) {\n                System.out.println(\"Final commit failed: \" + e.getMessage());\n            } finally {\n                consumer.close();\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern 2: Exactly-Once Semantics with External State\n\n```java\npublic class ExactlyOnceConsumer {\n    private Database db;\n\n    public void consume() {\n        KafkaConsumer<String, String> consumer = createConsumer();\n\n        try {\n            while (true) {\n                ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n\n                for (ConsumerRecord<String, String> record : records) {\n                    // Atomic transaction: store result + offset\n                    db.beginTransaction();\n                    try {\n                        processAndStore(record);\n                        db.storeOffset(record.topic(), record.partition(), record.offset() + 1);\n                        db.commit();\n                    } catch (Exception e) {\n                        db.rollback();\n                        throw e;\n                    }\n                }\n            }\n        } finally {\n            consumer.close();\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern 3: Consumer Health Monitoring\n\n```java\npublic class MonitoredConsumer {\n    public static void main(String[] args) {\n        KafkaConsumer<String, String> consumer = createConsumer();\n        ScheduledExecutorService scheduler = Executors.newScheduledThreadPool(1);\n\n        // Monitor lag and membership\n        scheduler.scheduleAtFixedRate(() -> {\n            for (TopicPartition tp : consumer.assignment()) {\n                long position = consumer.position(tp);\n                Map<TopicPartition, Long> endOffsets = consumer.endOffsets(\n                    Collections.singletonList(tp)\n                );\n                long lag = endOffsets.get(tp) - position;\n\n                OptionalLong currentLag = consumer.currentLag(tp);\n                System.out.printf(\n                    \"%s: position=%d, lag=%d%n\",\n                    tp,\n                    position,\n                    currentLag.isPresent() ? currentLag.getAsLong() : lag\n                );\n            }\n        }, 0, 10, TimeUnit.SECONDS);\n\n        try {\n            while (true) {\n                ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n                for (ConsumerRecord<String, String> record : records) {\n                    processRecord(record);\n                }\n                consumer.commitAsync();\n            }\n        } finally {\n            scheduler.shutdown();\n            consumer.close();\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern 4: Slow Processing with Pause/Resume\n\n```java\npublic class PauseResumePattern {\n    public static void main(String[] args) {\n        KafkaConsumer<String, String> consumer = createConsumer();\n        ExecutorService executor = Executors.newFixedThreadPool(1);\n        Future<?> processingTask = null;\n        boolean paused = false;\n\n        try {\n            while (true) {\n                ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n\n                if (!records.isEmpty() && processingTask == null) {\n                    // Pause to avoid receiving more records\n                    consumer.pause(consumer.assignment());\n                    paused = true;\n\n                    // Submit batch for processing\n                    processingTask = executor.submit(() -> {\n                        processBatch(records);\n                    });\n                } else if (processingTask != null && processingTask.isDone()) {\n                    // Resume when batch processing completes\n                    processingTask = null;\n                    consumer.resume(consumer.assignment());\n                    paused = false;\n                }\n\n                // Commit when processing done\n                if (processingTask != null && processingTask.isDone()) {\n                    consumer.commitAsync();\n                }\n            }\n        } finally {\n            if (paused) {\n                consumer.resume(consumer.assignment());\n            }\n            executor.shutdown();\n            consumer.close();\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Pattern 5: Regex Subscription with Pattern Monitoring\n\n```java\npublic class RegexSubscriptionPattern {\n    public static void main(String[] args) {\n        KafkaConsumer<String, String> consumer = createConsumer();\n\n        // Subscribe to topics matching pattern\n        consumer.subscribe(Pattern.compile(\"events-.*\"));\n\n        ScheduledExecutorService scheduler = Executors.newScheduledThreadPool(1);\n\n        // Monitor new matching topics\n        scheduler.scheduleAtFixedRate(() -> {\n            Set<String> subscribed = consumer.subscription();\n            System.out.println(\"Currently subscribed to topics: \" + subscribed);\n        }, 0, 30, TimeUnit.SECONDS);\n\n        try {\n            while (true) {\n                ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n\n                for (ConsumerRecord<String, String> record : records) {\n                    System.out.printf(\n                        \"Topic: %s, Offset: %d, Value: %s%n\",\n                        record.topic(),\n                        record.offset(),\n                        record.value()\n                    );\n                }\n\n                consumer.commitAsync();\n            }\n        } finally {\n            scheduler.shutdown();\n            consumer.close();\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Best Practices Summary\n\n1. **Always use rebalance listeners with subscriptions** for proper offset management\n2. **Keep the poll loop tight** - poll frequently, process records asynchronously\n3. **Prefer `commitSync()` after processing** for safety; use `commitAsync()` for throughput\n4. **Never hold partitions without polling** - consumer will be removed from group\n5. **Use `pause()`/`resume()` for flow control**, not `unsubscribe()`\n6. **Implement proper shutdown** with `wakeup()` and final `commitSync()`\n7. **Monitor lag and rebalancing** for operational visibility\n8. **Handle `CommitFailedException`** gracefully - it signals loss of group membership\n9. **Use `read_committed` isolation level** for transactional safety\n10. **Test rebalancing behavior** - ensure callbacks are correct\n11. **Consider external offset storage** for exactly-once semantics\n12. **Size batches for `max.poll.interval.ms`** to avoid removal from group\n\n---\n\n## Summary of Key Behavioral Semantics\n\n### Offset Semantics\n- **Position** (next to fetch) vs **Committed** (stored for restart)\n- Committed offset should be **next offset to read** (one past last processed)\n- `ConsumerRecords.nextOffsets()` provides the correct committed offset\n\n### Rebalancing Semantics\n- Only detected/executed during `poll()`\n- Callbacks run synchronously within `poll()` call\n- `onPartitionsRevoked()` called before partition migration\n- `onPartitionsAssigned()` called after acquisition\n- Can block arbitrary duration during rebalance\n\n### Group Membership\n- Join happens on first `poll()`, not during `subscribe()`\n- Proactive leave if `poll()` not called within `max.poll.interval.ms`\n- Heartbeats sent independently by background thread\n- Group coordinator can change, triggering rebalance\n\n### Isolation Levels\n- **read_uncommitted**: All messages (including in-flight transactions)\n- **read_committed**: Only committed messages, read up to LSO\n\n### Error Recovery\n- `CommitFailedException`: Fatal - consumer lost group membership\n- `RecordDeserializationException`: Non-fatal - record skipped\n- `WakeupException`: Expected on shutdown - not an error\n- Transient errors are retried internally\n\n---\n\n**Document Version**: 1.0\n**Last Updated**: February 2026\n**Based on**: Apache Kafka Latest Version\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":10,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2168,"cache_read_input_tokens":54276,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2168},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"64cf8ba4-f01d-4671-964f-31297423482a","uuid":"4ad1e472-5d24-4985-90f5-7a14f94a2e0e"}
